<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Portal:Current events/January 2004</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b><a href="/wiki/January" title="January">January</a></b> <b><a href="/wiki/2004" title="2004">2004</a></b> was the first month of that leap year. The month, which began on a <a href="/wiki/Thursday" title="Thursday">Thursday</a>, ended on a <a href="/wiki/Saturday" title="Saturday">Saturday</a> after 31 days.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Portal:Current_events"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Current_events" title="Portal:Current events">Portal:Current events</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Portal:Current events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>This is an <a href="/wiki/Portal:Current_events/How_to_archive_the_portal" title="Portal:Current events/How to archive the portal">archived version</a> of Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Portal:Current_events" title="Portal:Current events">Current events Portal</a> from January 2004.</i></p>

<td style="vertical-align:top;">
<div id="2004_January_1"></div>
<div id="2004_January_01"></div>
<table class="vevent" style="width:100%; margin:7px 0px; padding:2px; background-color:white; border:1px #cef2e0 solid;">
<tr>
<td>
<table cellspacing="0" class="plainlinks" style="background-color:#cef2e0" width="100%">
<tr>
<td style="text-align:left;font-size:11pt; font-weight:bold; padding:5px; margin-left:0px; width:100%"><span class="summary"><span style="display:none;">Current events of</span> January 1, 2004<span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2004-01-01</span>)</span> (Thursday)</span></td>
<td style="text-align:right;font-weight:bold; padding:5px; margin-left:0px"><small class="editlink noprint"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/2004_January_1&amp;action=edit&amp;editintro=Portal:Current_events/Edit_instructions">edit</a></small></td>
<td style="text-align:right;font-weight:bold; padding:5px; margin-left:0px"><small class="editlink noprint"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/2004_January_1&amp;action=history">history</a></small></td>
<td style="text-align:right;font-weight:bold; padding:5px; margin-left:0px"><small class="editlink noprint"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/2004_January_1&amp;action=watch">watch</a></small></td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="description">
<dl>
<dt>Arts and culture</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Montréal/Dorval International Airport is renamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montr%C3%A9al-Pierre_Elliott_Trudeau_International_Airport" title="Montréal-Pierre Elliott Trudeau International Airport">Montréal/Pierre Elliott Trudeau International Airport</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MySpace" title="MySpace">MySpace</a> had its official launch.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Disasters and accidents</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> flight from London to Washington, D.C. is canceled one day after the same flight is delayed for three hours on the tarmac at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dulles_International_Airport" title="Dulles International Airport">Dulles International Airport</a> for security screening. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=514&amp;e=1&amp;u=/ap/20040101/ap_on_re_eu/britain_flight_canceled" rel="nofollow">(Yahoo)</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>International relations</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>State papers released under Britain's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thirty_Year_Rule" title="Thirty Year Rule">Thirty Year Rule</a> suggest that the United States considered using force to seize oil fields in the Middle East during an oil <a href="/wiki/Embargo" title="Embargo">embargo</a> by Arab states in 1973. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3333995.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> State papers also released reveal that, contrary to what was believed at the time, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Margaret of the United Kingdom">Princess Margaret of the United Kingdom</a> would not have lost her title and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_List" title="Civil List">Civil List</a> payments if she had married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_Captain" title="Group Captain">Group Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Townsend_(RAF_officer)" title="Peter Townsend (RAF officer)">Peter Townsend</a>, a divorced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">War</a> hero in the 1950s. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk/3363809.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.sky.com/skynews/article/0,,30000-12964688,00.html" rel="nofollow">(Sky News)</a></li>
<li>Comparing planned United States finger-printing and photographic security controls on travelers from Brazil and other nations to <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> actions, a Brazilian judge orders the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fingerprinting" title="Fingerprinting">fingerprinting</a> of all arriving United States citizens in response. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=564&amp;ncid=564&amp;e=1&amp;u=/nm/20040101/ts_nm/brazil_usa_immigration_dc" rel="nofollow">(Yahoo)</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Law and crime</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>'s bicentennial celebrations erupt in violence. <a class="external text" href="http://www.jamaicaobserver.com/news/html/20040102T230000-0500_53845_OBS_CALM_RETURNS_TO_HAITI_AFTER_CLASHES_AT_BICENTENNIAL_CELEBRATIONS.asp" rel="nofollow">(Jamaica Observer)</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Politics and elections</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> takes over the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, succeeding Italy, whose presidency is widely criticised as having been a failure due to the collapse of efforts to adopt a European constitution. <a class="external text" href="http://www.rte.ie/news/2004/0101/eu.html" rel="nofollow">(RTE News)</a></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Religion</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Ireland's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Scouting_Ireland" title="Scouting Ireland">Boy Scouts</a> organisations merge after nearly a century of division, in spite of efforts by the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">bishops</a> to block the merger.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Science and technology</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>No <a href="/wiki/Leap_second" title="Leap second">leap second</a> is added this year. This is the fifth year in a row without a leap-second after 28 years of adding leap-seconds to compensate for the slowing of the Earth's rotation. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/TECH/science/01/01/leap.second.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>

<div id="2004_January_02"></div>

<td style="text-align:right;font-weight:bold; padding:5px; margin-left:0px"><small class="editlink noprint"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/2004_January_2&amp;action=edit&amp;editintro=Portal:Current_events/Edit_instructions">edit</a></small></td>

<tr>
<td class="description">
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SAARC" title="SAARC">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a>, composed of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">foreign ministers</a> from seven south Asian countries (<a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, India, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>) meeting in <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a> agree to create the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Free_Trade_Area" title="South Asian Free Trade Area">South Asian Free Trade Area</a> (SAFTA) by 2006. <a class="external text" href="http://www.ndtv.com/template/template.asp?template=Indopakfaceoff&amp;slug=Foreign+Ministers+clear+SAFTA+draft&amp;id=13501&amp;callid=0&amp;category=National" rel="nofollow">(NDTV)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Representative" title="U.S. Representative">U.S. Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Hall" title="Ralph Hall">Ralph Hall</a> from <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> files for reelection and switches parties from <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> to <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=/news/archive/2004/01/02/national1903EST0642.DTL" rel="nofollow">(SFGate)</a></li>
<li>It appears that <a href="/wiki/Stardust_(spacecraft)" title="Stardust (spacecraft)">Stardust</a> has successfully flown past <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comet_Wild_2" title="Comet Wild 2">Comet Wild 2</a> collecting samples that it will return to Earth in two years time. This is the first sample return mission to a comet and the first time that samples have returned to Earth from any celestial body since 1974. The spacecraft also took detailed images of the comet's icy nucleus. <a class="external text" href="http://stardust.jpl.nasa.gov/news/status/031230.html" rel="nofollow">(Stardust)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://spaceflightnow.com/stardust/040102image.html" rel="nofollow">(Space Flight Now)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.space.com/scienceastronomy/stardust_update_040102.html" rel="nofollow">(Space.com)</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_3.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">January 3, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: January 3, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flash_Airlines_Flight_604" title="Flash Airlines Flight 604">Flight 604</a>, flown by Egyptian charter company <a href="/wiki/Flash_Airlines" title="Flash Airlines">Flash Airlines</a> headed for <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> crashes into the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> minutes after take-off from the holiday resort of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sharm_el-Sheikh" title="Sharm el-Sheikh">Sharm el-Sheikh</a> in Egypt. All 148 people on board are killed, of whom more than 120 were French tourists. Though both United Kingdom Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and Egyptian President <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a> were in the area, neither were involved in the incident, contrary to initial reports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> cancels the appearance of <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> sponsorship credits in the music charts in its <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> show, after criticism from politicians and health campaigners that it would be promoting <a href="/wiki/Junk_food" title="Junk food">junk food</a> and unhealthy drink products to teenagers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li>Ricardo Palmera, better known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simon_Trinidad" title="Simon Trinidad">Simon Trinidad</a>, one of top seven <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombian</a> rebel group, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">FARC</a> (Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia) is arrested in <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: The first of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover_Mission" title="Mars Exploration Rover Mission">Mars Exploration Rovers</a>, Spirit, has successfully landed on the <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Martian</a> surface with a "very strong signal" being received from the lander. It was a tense few minutes as no signal was received from the lander during the minutes while it bounced over the surface. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Control" title="Mission Control">Mission Control</a> is described as being a wild place with the mission scientists very happy. The first pictures are expected at the earliest around 0730 UTC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceflightnow1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-spaceflightnow1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>The People's Republic of China's fifth-largest brokerage is seized by <a href="/wiki/China_Securities_Regulatory_Commission" title="China Securities Regulatory Commission">China Securities Regulatory Commission</a> and local authorities for "illegal and irregular management operations and disorderly management." The unusual move to clamp down on <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=China_Southern_Securities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="China Southern Securities (page does not exist)">China Southern Securities</a> is a high-profile attempt to stem corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_4.2C_2004_.28Sunday.29">January 4, 2004 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: January 4, 2004 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loya_jirga_(2003)" title="Loya jirga (2003)">Loya jirga</a> adopts a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Afghanistan" title="Constitution of Afghanistan">Constitution of Afghanistan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_court" title="Military court">military court</a> in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> sentences five Israelis to one year in <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">jail</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refusal_to_serve_in_the_Israeli_military" title="Refusal to serve in the Israeli military">refusing to serve in the military</a> because of Israel's occupation of the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> (Compare <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objector</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: American <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> probe "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover_Mission" title="Mars Exploration Rover Mission">Spirit</a>" mission is successful and is sending back images. Spirit is alive after rolling to a stop on the surface of Mars; confirmed by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Network" title="Deep Space Network">Deep Space Network</a> (<span class="nowrap">9:00 p.m.</span> PST).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikhail_Saakashvili" title="Mikhail Saakashvili">Mikhail Saakashvili</a> becomes president-elect of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Georgian presidential election, 2004">Presidential elections</a>. He had been widely expected to win following the November 23, 2003, ousting of President <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_Gas_War" title="Bolivian Gas War">Bolivian Gas War</a>: In a televised speech, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivian</a> President <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mesa" title="Carlos Mesa">Carlos Mesa</a> announces that a national referendum will be held on 28 March to resolve the issue of how Bolivia's large natural gas reserves will be exploited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> abruptly marries a childhood friend, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jason_Allen_Alexander" title="Jason Allen Alexander">Jason Allen Alexander</a>, in a <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> wedding chapel at <span class="nowrap">5:30 a.m.</span>; by afternoon, the couple have arranged an annulment, which is expected to be made official when the courts reopen on Monday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_5.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">January 5, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: January 5, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>A British and a German <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Member of the European Parliament</a> both receive letter bombs in the post. This follows an earlier letter bomb sent to the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionist_Party" title="Ulster Unionist Party">Ulster Unionist Party</a> defector <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Donaldson" title="Jeffrey Donaldson">Jeffrey Donaldson</a> and two other MLAs join Rev. <a href="/wiki/Ian_Paisley" title="Ian Paisley">Ian Paisley</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">Democratic Unionist Party</a>, pushing the DUP's numbers in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> to 33.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jaap_de_Hoop_Scheffer" title="Jaap de Hoop Scheffer">Jaap de Hoop Scheffer</a> of the Netherlands became the new Secretary General of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, replacing Britain's <a href="/wiki/George_Robertson,_Baron_Robertson_of_Port_Ellen" title="George Robertson, Baron Robertson of Port Ellen">Lord Robertson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li>The United States begins tracking foreign arrivals according to the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Visitor_and_Immigrant_Status_Indicator_Technology" title="United States Visitor and Immigrant Status Indicator Technology">United States Visitor and Immigrant Status Indicator Technology</a> (US-VISIT) program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li>Pakistan President <a href="/wiki/Pervez_Musharraf" title="Pervez Musharraf">Pervez Musharraf</a> and Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee" title="Atal Bihari Vajpayee">Atal Bihari Vajpayee</a> meet face-to-face to discuss improving relations between their two countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> (SAARC), which comprises India, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>, signs the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Asia_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="South Asia Free Trade Agreement">South Asia Free Trade Agreement</a>, a draft agreement to eliminate <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> by 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li>Norwegian prosecutors announce that they have abandoned their attempts to prosecute <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jon_Johansen" title="Jon Johansen">Jon Johansen</a> for his release of the <a href="/wiki/DeCSS" title="DeCSS">DeCSS</a> <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> decryption software.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a>, the ruling political party of Greece, is about to change leadership. The official report is expected to be published on January 7, 2004. It is expected by many that the new leader will be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Papandreou,_junior" title="George Papandreou, junior">George Papandreou, junior</a>. See<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> (Greek)</li>
<li>A potential local root vulnerability<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> has been found in <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> 2.2, 2.4, and 2.6, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linux_Kernel" title="Linux Kernel">Linux Kernel</a> developers have corrected the issue in 2.4 and 2.6; distributors are expected to offer the patches soon, for the benefit of those users who do not compile their own kernels.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_6.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">January 6, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: January 6, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The man charged for the murder of Sweden's FM <a href="/wiki/Anna_Lindh" title="Anna Lindh">Anna Lindh</a> on September 10, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mijailo_Mijailovic" title="Mijailo Mijailovic">Mijailo Mijailovic</a>, through his defence lawyer requests an <a href="/wiki/Interrogation" title="Interrogation">interrogation</a> to give critical details on the stabbing. Seemingly Mijailovic thereby confesses the assault.</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i>, a British tabloid, publishes the blacked out portion of a letter wherein <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a> alleged that someone was trying to kill her. The relevant portion reads: "[M]y husband is planning 'an accident' in my car, brake failure &amp; serious head injury in order to make the path clear for him to marry." The part "my husband" (referring to <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Charles, Prince of Wales</a>) had been previously blacked out, and the word "him" replaced with "Charles" in transcripts of the letter released by Diana's butler, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Burrell" title="Paul Burrell">Paul Burrell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The revelation comes on the same day the inquest into the death of Diana and her lover <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dodi_Al-Fayed" title="Dodi Al-Fayed">Dodi Al-Fayed</a> is officially opened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>Pakistan is cited as the source of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapon</a> technology supplied to <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>. The components intercepted at sea by Italy en route to Libya were fabricated in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. There is no evidence that the Pakistani government of President <a href="/wiki/Pervez_Musharraf" title="Pervez Musharraf">Pervez Musharraf</a> knew about the transfer of technology of Libya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gulf-news1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-gulf-news1-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>Pakistan and India have agreed to a new round of talks to settle the <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> dispute. The talks will be begin February 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gulf-news1_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-gulf-news1-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: The first color images have been released from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MER-A" title="MER-A">Spirit</a> rover on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>. They are the highest <a href="/wiki/Image_resolution" title="Image resolution">resolution</a> images ever taken on the surface of another planet. It has also been announced by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> that they plan to name the rover's landing site on Mars "Columbia Memorial Station" in honor of the crew of <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">STS-107</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_7.2C_2004_.28Wednesday.29">January 7, 2004 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: January 7, 2004 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush administration</a> proposes a major reform of immigration law, creating a temporary worker program and giving legal status to both illegal and foreign workers for renewable three-year periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Supreme Court of <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> upholds the death sentence handed down to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2002_Bali_terrorist_bombing" title="2002 Bali terrorist bombing">Bali bomber</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amrozi" title="Amrozi">Amrozi</a>. The 12 October 2002 attacks killed 202 mainly holiday makers on the resort island of <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <a class="external text" href="http://www.smh.com.au/articles/2004/01" rel="nofollow">July 1073437329581.html</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Costas_Simitis" title="Costas Simitis">Costas Simitis</a>, the prime minister of Greece and president of the ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">PASOK</a>, after informing the country's president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Costis_Stephanopoulos" title="Costis Stephanopoulos">Costis Stephanopoulos</a>, announced his resignation. At the same time he announced <a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_2004" title="Greek legislative election, 2004">national elections</a> for March 7, 2004, when PASOK will have a new president, expected to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Papandreou,_junior" title="George Papandreou, junior">George Papandreou</a>. PASOK will be challenged by the <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a> opposition led by <a href="/wiki/Kostas_Karamanlis" title="Kostas Karamanlis">Kostas Karamanlis</a>. See,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> (Greek) and,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> (English).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: <a href="/wiki/Mars_Express" title="Mars Express">Mars Express</a> failed to hear any signal from the <a href="/wiki/Beagle_2" title="Beagle 2">Beagle 2</a> spacecraft during its first pass over the landing site. This is major blow, but scientists have once again not given up all hope. They will attempt again tomorrow using a different communication mode. The Beagle 2 mission manager, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Pillinger" title="Colin Pillinger">Colin Pillinger</a>, set February 7 as the day to abandon contact efforts. By that time Beagle 2 would have switched into an autotransmit mode after having not received any signal for over a month if it was still alive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li>A report from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> expresses alarm regarding mounting budget deficits in the United States due to recession, tax cuts, and spending for the war on terrorism. The report says that the unprecedented level of external debt incurred poses "significant risks" not just for the United States but for the rest of the world. However, many outside economists note that other countries are also running large deficits and that underlying economic conditions in the U.S. are still robust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-invasion_Iraq,_2003%E2%80%93present" title="Post-invasion Iraq, 2003–present">U.S.-led occupation of Iraq</a>: <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">Mortar</a> attacks by Anti-American insurgents wound 35 U.S. soldiers at a military camp west of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. Six mortar rounds exploded around <span class="nowrap">6:45 p.m.</span> local time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_8.2C_2004_.28Thursday.29">January 8, 2004 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: January 8, 2004 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/RMS_Queen_Mary_2" title="RMS Queen Mary 2"><i>Queen Mary 2</i></a> is christened by Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RT%C3%89" title="RTÉ">RTÉ</a> <i>Prime Time</i> investigation accuses the <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda Síochána">Garda Síochána</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>'s police force, of violent abuse of people arrested. Irish <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_(Ireland)" title="Minister of State (Ireland)">Minister of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Dick_Roche" title="Dick Roche">Dick Roche</a> accuses Gardaí of "torture" of one student beaten up in a <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> police station, while a former judge accuses police of committing <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> in his courts. The Gardaí deny all allegations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>The United States withdraws a group of 400 weapons inspectors from <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> after finding nothing of substance. 1400 inspectors remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: Nine United States soldiers are reported killed after a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UH-60_Black_Hawk" title="UH-60 Black Hawk">Black Hawk</a> helicopter makes an emergency landing near the central Iraqi town of Falluja.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Endowment_for_International_Peace" title="Carnegie Endowment for International Peace">Carnegie Endowment for International Peace</a> publishes a report accusing the United States of "systematically misrepresenting" the threat posed by "Iraq's weapons of mass destruction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> legislature passes a bill creating a <a href="/wiki/Domestic_partnership" title="Domestic partnership">domestic partnership</a> status for <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">same-sex</a> couples, with many of the same legal rights as marriage. It becomes the fifth U.S. state to offer such a status to same-sex couples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_9.2C_2004_.28Friday.29">January 9, 2004 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: January 9, 2004 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Greece" title="Education in Greece">Education in Greece</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Papandreou,_junior" title="George Papandreou, junior">George Papandreou, junior</a> talks about the possibility to allow private universities in Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> (Greek)</li>
<li>Turkey fully abolishes the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">death penalty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>The US lowers the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security_Advisory_System" title="Department of Homeland Security Advisory System">terrorism advisory</a> level to yellow (elevated) from orange (high).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> bans books published by the <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> movement, an Islamic sect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: Engineers at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JPL" title="JPL">JPL</a> decide to turn the Mars <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MER-A" title="MER-A">Spirit Rover</a> around on its lander after it was found the airbags could not be retracted enough to allow it to move off in a forward direction. It is expected the rover will drive off sometime next week. The Rover has also stood up and deployed its front wheels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceflightnow1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-spaceflightnow1-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>Two <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a> erupt: the <a href="/wiki/Piton_de_la_Fournaise" title="Piton de la Fournaise">Piton de la Fournaise</a> on <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> Island, and the <a href="/wiki/Volc%C3%A1n_de_Fuego" title="Volcán de Fuego">Volcán de Fuego</a> near <a href="/wiki/Antigua_Guatemala" title="Antigua Guatemala">Antigua Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>. The eruption in Guatemala is not thought to be serious enough to require evacuations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a>, fifteen people die and twenty are hurt when a public bus collides with a crane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enron_Corporation" title="Enron Corporation">Enron Corporation</a>: Former Assistant Treasurer <a href="/wiki/Lea_Fastow" title="Lea Fastow">Lea Fastow</a> and wife of <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Fastow" title="Andrew Fastow">Andrew Fastow</a>, failed to respond to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plea_agreement" title="Plea agreement">plea agreement</a> by the deadline. The offer would have allowed her to plead guilty in federal court to lesser charges and serve five months in return for her testimony. Her trial for conspiracy to commit wire fraud, money laundering, and tax evasion is scheduled to start February 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_10.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">January 10, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: January 10, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: Protests in the city of <a href="/wiki/Amarah" title="Amarah">Amarah</a> because of <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> occur. Police officers and soldiers open fire on demonstrators. Five or six are killed and one or eleven wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2004_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2004-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>In publicity for a new book for which former U.S. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">Treasury Secretary</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_O%27Neill_(businessman)" title="Paul O'Neill (businessman)">Paul O'Neill</a> is the primary source, <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a></i> reveals O'Neill's claims that the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush</a> administration was making plans for an <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a> within days of Bush's <a href="/wiki/Inauguration" title="Inauguration">inauguration</a>. Bush officials note that <a href="/wiki/Regime_change" title="Regime change">regime change</a> in Iraq had been official U.S. policy since 1998, three years before Bush took office. O'Neill, fired for his opposition to <a href="/wiki/Jobs_and_Growth_Tax_Relief_Reconciliation_Act_of_2003" title="Jobs and Growth Tax Relief Reconciliation Act of 2003">tax cuts</a>, also characterized Bush as so disengaged in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Cabinet" title="United States Cabinet">cabinet meetings</a> that he "was like a blind man in a roomful of deaf people". On the positive side, O'Neill also described Bush as such a good listener that he (O'Neill) was able to give a non-stop monologue for nearly an hour in a one-on-one meeting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SCO_v._IBM" title="SCO v. IBM">SCO v. IBM</a></i>: <a href="/wiki/SCO_Group" title="SCO Group">SCO Group</a> claims that it has "low-level talks" with <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> about a possible license agreement related to <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iraq_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Iraq and weapons of mass destruction">Iraq and weapons of mass destruction</a>: On January 9, 2004, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Denmark" title="Military of Denmark">Danish troops</a> discovered decade-old <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> rounds containing suspicious liquid buried in Southern <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. Initial tests now indicate that the rounds contain the banned <a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">chemical weapon</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blister_gas" title="Blister gas">blister gas</a>. Final tests should be available in two days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li>A speed boat carrying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrants" title="Illegal immigrants">illegal immigrants</a> from <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, bound for Italy broke down and capsized. There were 11 survivors, while as many as 21 died due to drowning and exposure. Two have been arrested by Albanian authorities for <a href="/wiki/People_smuggling" title="People smuggling">people smuggling</a>, while other senior officials have been implicated in connection with the tragedy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_11.2C_2004_.28Sunday.29">January 11, 2004 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: January 11, 2004 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MER-A" title="MER-A">Spirit</a></i> rover now has its arm and all six of its wheels free, and only a single cable must be cut before it can turn and roll off its lander onto the soil of Mars. As that milestone is completed, scientists are taking opportunities to take extra pictures and gather other data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>U.S. military records show that attacks against coalition soldiers have decreased by 22% in the four weeks following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capture_of_Saddam_Hussein" title="Capture of Saddam Hussein">capture of Saddam Hussein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>More protests in <a href="/wiki/Amarah" title="Amarah">Amarah</a> take place. Demonstrators, many of them related to the victims of January 10, requested compensation. No significant violence reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2004_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2004-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_12.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">January 12, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: January 12, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">U.S. Patent and Trademark Office</a> announces the <a href="/wiki/List_of_top_United_States_patent_recipients" title="List of top United States patent recipients">ten top United States patent recipients</a>. For the 11th year in a row, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> tops the list; the next three in the list are headquartered in Japan. Companies from the Netherlands (<a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>) and Korea (<a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>) also make appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_State_Department" title="United States State Department">U.S. State Department</a> concludes that the <a href="/wiki/USS_Liberty_incident" title="USS Liberty incident">Israeli attack on USS <i>Liberty</i></a> in 1967, although probably accidental, was an act of gross negligence and that Israel should be held responsible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canadian_federal_election,_2004" title="Canadian federal election, 2004">Canadian federal election, 2004</a>: <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Harper" title="Stephen Harper">Stephen Harper</a> announces his entry into the race to lead the new <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party of Canada</a>. Earlier today, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Prentice" title="Jim Prentice">Jim Prentice</a> drops out of the leadership contest, citing a lack of funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: Over 100,000 people rally in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> to <a href="/wiki/Protest" title="Protest">protest</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">Ariel Sharon</a>'s plans to withdraw from parts of <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, which would involve abandoning some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_settlements" title="Israeli settlements">Israeli settlements</a> in those areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li>The deadline for <a href="/wiki/SCO_Group" title="SCO Group">SCO Group</a> to present evidence "with specificity" in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SCO_v._IBM_Linux_lawsuit" title="SCO v. IBM Linux lawsuit">SCO v. IBM</a></i> lawsuit expires</li>
<li>IBM and Intel Set Up $10m SCO Defense Fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li>Astronauts on board the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> think that a leak in a hose used to stop the fogging of an Earth observation window was causing the slow loss of pressure in the station. Although it would have taken a couple of months for the crew to be in any danger, some equipment on the station was only rated to just below the normal pressure. Although the cause appears to have been located, ground controllers are still getting the crew to close the station into three sections to allow them to get baseline pressure readings and to make sure that there are no more leaks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>'s provincial governors are threatening to resign unless a decision by the conservative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Guardians" title="Council of Guardians">Guardian Council</a> is reversed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover_Mission" title="Mars Exploration Rover Mission">Mars Exploration Rover Mission</a>: The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MER-A" title="MER-A">Spirit</a></i>'s air bags that cushioned its landing on Mars have been obstructing the vehicle's path, and this complication has postponed its exit of the launch vehicle until Wednesday or Thursday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>-UK reports that the <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutan</a> is in danger of becoming <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinct</a> within the next 20 years because of commercial <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a> and clearance for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_palm" title="Oil palm">oil palm</a> <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ayatollah" title="Ayatollah">Ayatollah</a> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Khamenei" title="Ali Khamenei">Ali Khamenei</a>, religious leader of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, announces that he will not intervene in a growing political confrontation between progressives and hardliners after the Guardian Council, which he controls, barred thousands of candidates from running in upcoming Parliamentary elections (including 80 current members of Parliament).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_13.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">January 13, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: January 13, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_Conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian Conflict">Israeli-Palestinian Conflict</a>: <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hurndall" title="Tom Hurndall">Tom Hurndall</a>, a British peace activist with the <a href="/wiki/International_Solidarity_Movement" title="International Solidarity Movement">International Solidarity Movement</a>, dies after being shot in the head by an Israeli soldier on April 11, 2003. The Israeli government say that they may consider bringing <a href="/wiki/Manslaughter" title="Manslaughter">manslaughter</a> charges against the soldier; the man's family claim that he should be tried for murder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Greece" title="Education in Greece">Education in Greece</a>: Debate over the private universities issue and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Papandreou,_junior" title="George Papandreou, junior">George Papandreou, junior</a>'s suggestions (see 9 January) between <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">PASOK</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> (Greek)</li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_(Italy)" title="Constitutional Court (Italy)">Constitutional Court</a> of Italy strikes down a law enacted to give Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a> immunity from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prosecution" title="Prosecution">prosecution</a> while in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li>British <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">serial killer</a> Dr <a href="/wiki/Harold_Shipman" title="Harold Shipman">Harold Shipman</a> is found dead in his cell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bichard_Inquiry" title="Bichard Inquiry">Bichard Inquiry</a> into events preceding the <a href="/wiki/Soham_murders" title="Soham murders">Soham murders</a> formally opens<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: A United States Army] <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AH-64_Apache" title="AH-64 Apache">AH-64 Apache</a> attack helicopter is shot down near the central Iraqi town of Habbaniya, but is able to land without casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-40" title="Yakovlev Yak-40">Yak-40</a> <a href="/wiki/Airliner" title="Airliner">airliner</a> en route from <a href="/wiki/Termez" title="Termez">Termez</a> in <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> crashes near the capital <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, killing all 37 crew and passengers, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">U.N.</a>'s top official in the country, Richard Conroy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robin_Cook" title="Robin Cook">Robin Cook</a> says that the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Elgin_Marbles" title="Elgin Marbles">Parthenon Marbles</a> must be returned to Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> (Greek),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> (English),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> (Background, English)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_14.2C_2004_.28Wednesday.29">January 14, 2004 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: January 14, 2004 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_Chase" title="J.P. Morgan Chase">J.P. Morgan Chase</a> strikes a <span class="nowrap">$58 billion</span> merger deal to buy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_One" title="Bank One">Bank One</a> to create the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">bank</a> in the United States.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iraq_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Iraq and weapons of mass destruction">Iraq and weapons of mass destruction</a>: Tests performed by American and Danish military experts indicate no chemical agents are present in the "suspicious" <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> shells discovered in Iraq on January 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li>Self-confessed killer of Swedish FM <a href="/wiki/Anna_Lindh" title="Anna Lindh">Anna Lindh</a>, 25-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mijailo_Mijailovic" title="Mijailo Mijailovic">Mijailo Mijailovic</a>, says during cross-examination in a <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> court that he <a href="/wiki/Hallucination" title="Hallucination">heard voices</a> in his head commanding him to attack Lindh when he encountered her in a Stockholm shopping mall 10 September last year. Lindh died the next day from the many stab wounds she received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank" title="Federal Reserve Bank">Federal Reserve Bank</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Alan_Greenspan" title="Alan Greenspan">Alan Greenspan</a> said, "It's just a matter of time before we begin to see employment start to pick up quite significantly, as it always has in the past." Greenspan is also not worried about the fall of the dollar or the half trillion dollar U.S. trade deficit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>:
<ul>
<li>Reem El-Reyashi, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bomber</a>, kills four border guards at the <a href="/wiki/Erez_Crossing" title="Erez Crossing">Erez Crossing</a>. She is the first <a href="/wiki/Female_suicide_bomber" title="Female suicide bomber">female suicide bomber</a> used by <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>. Four months before, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> targeted Hamas leadership, including <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Yassin" title="Ahmed Yassin">Ahmed Yassin</a>, as a result Hamas halted all suicide bombing for four months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>Jack Kelley, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_TODAY" title="USA TODAY">USA TODAY</a> foreign correspondent and a finalist for a Pulitzer Prize just two years ago, was forced to resign after the newspaper determined he repeatedly misled editors during an internal investigation into stories he wrote. Among the stories that are being investigated is one published September 4, 2001, contains an account of an attack on Palestinians by 13 Jewish settlers in the West Bank. Mark Memmott, the reporter asked to investigate Kelley, said he could not find anyone with first-hand knowledge of the attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>A secondary school student in the Netherlands kills a teacher in his school cafeteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_electronic_game_ban" title="Greek electronic game ban">Greek electronic game ban</a>: Greek police raid Internet cafés in <a href="/wiki/Larissa" title="Larissa">Larissa</a>. 80 computers are taken by the police as evidence and three Internet café owners are arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> (in Greek).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Greece" title="Education in Greece">Education in Greece</a>: 114 University professors sign a document against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Papandreou,_junior" title="George Papandreou, junior">George Papandreou</a>'s positions on private universities and their recognition (<i>anagnorisi</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> (Greek)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Delors" title="Jacques Delors">Jacques Delors</a> referred to Prime Minister of Greece <a href="/wiki/Costas_Simitis" title="Costas Simitis">Costas Simitis</a>, Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a>, and former Prime Minister of Belgium Jean Luc Dehaene as the top three candidates for the position of the President of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li>A 45-year-old <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> man travelling from <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Washington Dulles International Airport</a> to airport <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> is arrested en route at London's <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> on suspicion of carrying five bullets in his coat pocket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, in a speech at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> headquarters, announces a plan to develop a new space vehicle to return humans to the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">moon</a> by 2015 and proposes the retirement of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle" title="Space shuttle">space shuttle</a> fleet by 2010 along with a <span class="nowrap">$1 billion</span> funding increase for NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enron_Corporation" title="Enron Corporation">Enron Corporation</a>: Former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CFO" title="CFO">CFO</a> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Fastow" title="Andrew Fastow">Andrew Fastow</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Lea_Fastow" title="Lea Fastow">Lea Fastow</a>, former Assistant Treasurer, accept a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plea_agreement" title="Plea agreement">plea agreement</a>. Andrew Fastow will serve a ten-year prison sentence and forfeit <span class="nowrap">$23.8 million</span>. Lea Fastow will serve a five-month prison sentence and a year of supervised release, including five months of house arrest. Both will provide testimony against other Enron corporate officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>Turkey and Greece: 22 Turkish military aircraft entered into the Greek <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_Information_Region" title="Flight Information Region">FIR</a>. Five of these aircraft were loaded with ammunition. Greek aircraft intercepted them. Source: <a href="/wiki/Athens_News_Agency" title="Athens News Agency">Athens News Agency</a> and <a href="/wiki/In.gr" title="In.gr">in.gr</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> (Greek)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_15.2C_2004_.28Thursday.29">January 15, 2004 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: January 15, 2004 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> sides with the United States on voting in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> and other UN officials call direct elections in advance of July 2004 impractical, due to continuing disorder in Iraq and other factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li>30,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shiite" title="Shiite">Shiite</a> protesters in <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a> call for immediate country-wide elections in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, a move that would give them more power than the UN-backed plan for regional <a href="/wiki/Caucus" title="Caucus">caucuses</a> mandated by the US-led coalition<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li>South Korea's foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Yoon_Young-kwan" title="Yoon Young-kwan">Yoon Young-kwan</a> resigns after a controversy in which his ministry was accused of diverging from the government's policy of increased independence from the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> asks the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> for authorization to impose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_sanctions" title="Trade sanctions">trade sanctions</a> against the United States in response to the U.S.'s anti-<a href="/wiki/Dumping_(pricing_policy)" title="Dumping (pricing policy)">dumping</a> scheme, which has been ruled illegal by the WTO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canadian_federal_election,_2004" title="Canadian federal election, 2004">Canadian federal election, 2004</a>: Former <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> Health Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Clement" title="Tony Clement">Tony Clement</a> declares his candidacy for the leadership of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party of Canada</a>. Also confirmed is the candidacy of auto parts magnate <a href="/wiki/Belinda_Stronach" title="Belinda Stronach">Belinda Stronach</a>, who will announce her entry into the leadership race next week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>Italy has indicted three Germans, all former members of an <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">SS</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waffen-SS_Order_of_Battle" title="Waffen-SS Order of Battle">Panzergrenadier Division</a>, on charges of massacring 560 people in 1944 in the Italian village of <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Anna_di_Stazzema" title="Sant'Anna di Stazzema">Sant'Anna di Stazzema</a>. The three Germans, <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Sommer" title="Gerhard Sommer">Gerhard Sommer</a>, 83; <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alfred_Schonenberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alfred Schonenberg (page does not exist)">Alfred Schonenberg</a>, 83; and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ludwig_Sonntag&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ludwig Sonntag (page does not exist)">Ludwig Sonntag</a>, 80, are currently living in Germany. It is not clear whether Italy will request the three men's <a href="/wiki/Extradition" title="Extradition">extradition</a> from Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">U.S. presidential election, 2004</a>: <a href="/wiki/Carol_Moseley_Braun" title="Carol Moseley Braun">Carol Moseley Braun</a> drops out of the race and endorses Dr. <a href="/wiki/Howard_Dean" title="Howard Dean">Howard Dean</a>, confirming rumors circulating the night before as she taped an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li>The date for the publication of the <a href="/wiki/Hutton_Inquiry" title="Hutton Inquiry">Hutton Inquiry</a>'s report into the death of British weapons scientist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr_David_Kelly" title="Dr David Kelly">Dr David Kelly</a> is announced as January 28, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li>The creditors of ailing Finnish <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Flying_Finn_(airline)" title="Flying Finn (airline)">Flying Finn</a> have threatened to confiscate the airline's planes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a>: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MER-A" title="MER-A">Spirit Rover</a> has rolled off its lander to start its exploration. The first journey was only three metres. It took the rover about 78 seconds, ending with the back of the rover being 0.7 metres from the lander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium" title="World Wide Web Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium (W3C)</a> announces the release of the <a href="/wiki/Composite_Capability/Preference_Profiles" title="Composite Capability/Preference Profiles">Composite Capability/Preference Profiles</a> (CC/PP 1.0). W3C's new standard profiling language CC/PP provides a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_standard" title="Internet standard">standardized</a> format of the description of information that will allow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWW" title="WWW">Web</a>-enabled devices to effectively communicate their capabilities to the desired <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">server</a> and aids in delivering Web content to broad range of devices.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Popeye" title="Popeye">Popeye</a></i>, like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Tintin" title="The Adventures of Tintin">The Adventures of Tintin</a></i>, turns 75 this month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_16.2C_2004_.28Friday.29">January 16, 2004 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: January 16, 2004 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> makes a televised address reiterating the <a href="/wiki/Four_Noes_and_One_Without" title="Four Noes and One Without">Four Noes and One Without</a> pledge and announcing the two questions for a referendum to coincide with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ROC_presidential_election,_2004" title="ROC presidential election, 2004">ROC presidential election, 2004</a> on March 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></li>
<li>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> appoints <a href="/wiki/Charles_W._Pickering" title="Charles W. Pickering">Charles Pickering</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals" title="United States Court of Appeals">United States Court of Appeals</a>. His nomination was <a href="/wiki/Filibuster" title="Filibuster">filibustered</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senate</a>, so President Bush made a <a href="/wiki/Recess_appointment" title="Recess appointment">recess appointment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bam,_Iran" title="Bam, Iran">Earthquake in Iran</a>: Iran updates the death toll from the <a href="/wiki/Bam,_Iran" title="Bam, Iran">Bam</a> earthquake to 41,000 people. The final figure could be as high as 45,000.</li>
<li>The People's Republic of China arrests a top Hong Kong official into custody over suspicion of espionage for the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nunavut_general_election,_2004" title="Nunavut general election, 2004">Nunavut general election, 2004</a>: Premier <a href="/wiki/Paul_Okalik" title="Paul Okalik">Paul Okalik</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a>, Canada, requests a dissolution of the territory's legislature and an election call for February 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>On or around this date, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._public_debt" title="U.S. public debt">United States national debt</a> passes US$7 trillion.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_17.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">January 17, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: January 17, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Planned NASA servicing missions for the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> are cancelled. Safety concerns are cited as the main reason behind the decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Human_cloning" title="Human cloning">Human cloning</a>: Fertility expert Dr. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panos_Zavos" title="Panos Zavos">Panos Zavos</a> claims to have successfully transplanted a two-week-old embryo into a 35-year-old woman. He said he had not done the act anywhere where "the spirit of the law" was against such a procedure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Papandreou,_junior" title="George Papandreou, junior">George Papandreou</a> of Greece promised that he will suggest to sign a mutual agreement with Turkey for lowering their defense <a href="/wiki/Military" title="Military">military</a> expenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> (Greek).</li>
<li>Protesters call for resignation of German Federal Police chief Ulrich Kersten: about 6,000 people demonstrates against moving Germany's Federal Police (BKA) headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a> to Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_18.2C_2004_.28Sunday.29">January 18, 2004 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/January_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: January 18, 2004 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: At around <span class="nowrap">8 am</span> local time (<span class="nowrap">5 am</span> GMT) in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_resistance" title="Iraqi resistance">insurgent suicide bomber</a> driving a car filled with explosives blew himself up while attempting to enter "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Gate" title="Assassin's Gate">Assassin's Gate</a>." Early reports said that about 18 people, including 16 Iraqi civilians and two <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> workers were killed, while another 56 Iraqi civilians were wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li>Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">Ariel Sharon</a> praises the Israeli ambassador to Sweden, <a href="/wiki/Zvi_Mazel" title="Zvi Mazel">Zvi Mazel</a>, for vandalising the artwork entitled "<a href="/wiki/Snow_White_and_The_Madness_of_Truth" title="Snow White and The Madness of Truth">Snow White and The Madness of Truth</a>" displayed at a <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> museum. The piece, created by an Israeli-born composer/musician, consists of a white float carrying a picture of a Palestinian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bomber</a> in a pool of blood-coloured water. Mazel was caught on surveillance video disconnecting the electric power from the display and throwing a lamp into the water.
